## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and current concentration A. Classical rate laws express dA/dt as functions of concentration (power-law, rational forms), with possible explicit time dependence from external forcing or elimination of intermediate species.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- Nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with constant product concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturating kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Consecutive reaction (reduced): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (eliminated intermediate dependence)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * t (combined concentration and time effects)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood surface: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction with competitive adsorption)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Polynomial dependence on concentration → multiple competing reaction pathways of different orders (e.g., c0*A + c1*A**2 + c2*A**3)
- Rational functions of concentration → enzyme or surface catalysis with adsorption/saturation (Michaelis-Menten, Langmuir-Hinshelwood)
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior where both reactant and product participate
- Explicit time dependence combined with concentration → non-isothermal reactions, photochemistry, or systems with eliminated intermediates
- Negative rate proportional to A^n with n>0 → consumption/decay kinetics where species is being depleted
- Sum of exponentials in time multiplied by concentration powers → multi-step reaction mechanisms with quasi-steady-state approximations
- Square root or fractional power of A → dissociative equilibrium or half-order kinetics from radical chain mechanisms
- Denominator terms like (1 + c*A)^n → competitive inhibition or site-blocking effects in heterogeneous catalysis

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) is:
$$-0.731770189531933 \cdot A \cdot \exp(-0.0816213403667534 \cdot t) + 0.840340504979681 \cdot \cos(\log(A + 1))$$

This has two main terms:
1. A term proportional to $A \cdot \exp(\text{negative constant} \cdot t)$
2. A term proportional to $\cos(\log(A + 1))$

Note that $\cos(\log(A+1))$ is $\cos(1 \cdot \log(A \cdot 1 + 1))$.

This **exactly matches** the GT.
